###xml 526 531 526 531 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1<italic>e</italic>11 </sup>
###xml 542 544 542 544 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B </bold>
###xml 548 550 548 550 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C </bold>
###xml 567 570 567 570 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk</italic>
###xml 570 572 570 572 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">- </sup>
###xml 649 651 646 648 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B </bold>
###xml 655 657 652 654 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C </bold>
###xml 739 742 736 739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk</italic>
###xml 743 744 740 741 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e</italic>
###xml 742 747 739 744 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1<italic>e</italic>11 </sup>
###xml 803 810 800 807 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C Inset</bold>
###xml 815 817 812 814 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 817 819 814 816 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mr</italic>
###xml 817 821 814 818 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>mr</italic>1 </sup>
###xml 902 905 899 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk</italic>
###xml 906 907 903 904 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e</italic>
###xml 905 910 902 907 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1<italic>e</italic>11 </sup>
R7 cell development in ttk- mutant ommatidia is dependent upon Lz function. A. Projected confocal image of Runt labelled cells in a wild-type disc show one R8 cell per ommatidial cluster for approximately six rows posterior to the morphogenetic furrow (Mf; arrow). At row seven, Runt-expressing R7 cells are recruited to each ommatidium and Runt "doublets" are observed. B. In the ttk1e11 mutant ommatidia, ectopic Runt positive R7 cells are observed. C. Only single R8 cells are observed in developing ommatidia of lzmr1; ttk1e11 ommatidia. B and C show discs where ttk- clones occupied the majority of the eye disc (beta-galactosidase not shown). B and C (insets) show mosaic images, where ectopic Runt positive cells can be observed in ttk1e11 clonal patches (B inset; GFP negative clones outlined). C Inset. In lzmr1 mutant discs, R7 cells are not recruited to the ommatidia, and the generation of ttk1e11 clones in this background (outlined in inset) does not result in the recruitment of R7 precursor cells. Scale bars indicate 10 mum.
###end p 34
###begin title 35
###xml 58 61 58 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 88 90 88 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
Overexpression of Ttk69 results in the down-regulation of lz and the subsequent loss of lz-dependent cell types in the developing eye
###end title 35
###begin p 36
###xml 177 179 177 179 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 306 309 306 309 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 591 594 591 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 666 668 666 668 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 698 700 698 700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 700 703 700 703 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal</italic>
###xml 700 705 700 705 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Gal</italic>4 </sup>
###xml 712 722 712 722 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 764 766 764 766 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 847 849 847 849 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 849 852 849 852 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal</italic>
###xml 849 853 849 853 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Gal</italic>4</sup>
###xml 853 864 853 864 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 1058 1060 1058 1060 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
Our results have demonstrated that removal of Ttk69 function results in the development of ectopic R7 cells at the third instar developmental stage. These ectopic cells express lz-driven GFP, and are also dependent upon Lz function for their development. It is possible that Ttk69 may function to regulate lz expression levels in early eye development to prevent the ectopic development of R7 cells. Alternatively, these ectopic R7 cells may simply continue to express Lz because they are derived from the R7 equivalence group. We therefore examined whether Ttk69 has the ability to repress lz gene expression in the developing eye. First we over-expressed Ttk69 in lz-expressing cells by crossing lzGal4 into a UAS-ttk69 background and analysed the expression of lz-driven GFP along with the expression of specific presumptive cell fate markers. lzGal4;UAS-ttk69 adult eyes exhibited severely disrupted eyes that lacked ommatidial structure and also exhibited severe scarring (not shown). This adult phenotype alone suggests that overexpression of Ttk69 in lz-expressing cells is enough to prevent the correct development of these cells.
###end p 36
###begin p 37
###xml 20 22 20 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 55 57 55 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 57 60 57 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal</italic>
###xml 57 61 57 61 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Gal</italic>4</sup>
###xml 63 81 63 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-GFP;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 180 182 180 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 182 185 182 185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal</italic>
###xml 182 186 182 186 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Gal</italic>4</sup>
###xml 188 206 188 206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-GFP;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 321 325 321 325 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6A-B</xref>
###xml 342 345 342 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz-</italic>
Further analysis of lz-driven GFP in disc epithelia of lzGal4, UAS-GFP;UAS-ttk69 third instar larvae was undertaken. Single planar confocal images of undifferentiated cells in the lzGal4, UAS-GFP;UAS-ttk69 mutant disc epithelia showed that although less cells were present in this focal plane than in control discs (fig. 6A-B), the levels of lz-driven GFP expression did not appear to be reduced upon overexpression of Ttk69.
###end p 37

###begin p 39
###xml 106 109 106 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 237 239 237 239 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 240 242 240 242 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 243 245 243 245 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B54">54</xref>
###xml 253 255 253 255 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6C</xref>
###xml 313 315 313 315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 315 318 315 318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal</italic>
###xml 315 318 315 318 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Gal</italic></sup>
###xml 320 338 320 338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-GFP;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 360 362 360 362 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6D</xref>
###xml 369 371 369 371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
In neuronal and non-neuronal differentiating cells, specific antibodies were used in conjunction with the lz enhancer trap line to mark each cell type. Photoreceptors R1 and R6 were identified using an antibody against the Bar antigen ([40,53,54]; fig. 6C). Our results showed that Bar expression was lost in the lzGal, UAS-GFP;UAS-ttk69 disc epithelium (fig. 6D), and lz-driven GFP expression was severely depleted in the R1 and R6 cell plane.
###end p 39
###begin p 40
###xml 47 49 47 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 49 52 49 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal</italic>
###xml 49 52 49 52 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Gal</italic></sup>
###xml 54 72 54 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-GFP;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 139 142 139 142 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 200 205 200 205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6E, G</xref>
###xml 300 302 300 302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 388 393 388 393 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6F, H</xref>
###xml 535 540 535 540 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pros </italic>
###xml 544 548 544 548 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bar </italic>
###xml 639 642 639 642 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
To analyse R7 and cone cell development in the lzGal, UAS-GFP;UAS-ttk69 third instar disc epithelium, Pros was used in conjuction with the lz enhancer trap line to specifically mark these cells (fig. 6E, G). In the Ttk69 overexpression line, high magnification confocal imaging revealed few Pros and lz-driven GFP labelled R7 and cone cells in the developing third instar eye discs (fig. 6F, H). The depletion of other cell specific markers such as Runt in R7 cells and Cut in cone cells was also observed (data not shown). Since both pros and Bar are, in part, regulated by Lz, these results support the hypothesis that Ttk69 can repress lz gene expression in the developing eye.
###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 75 77 75 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 77 82 77 82 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal4 </sup>
###xml 208 211 208 211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 256 262 256 262 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk69 </italic>
###xml 459 461 459 461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 510 512 510 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 648 650 648 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 777 783 777 783 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">glass </italic>
###xml 840 846 840 846 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk69 </italic>
###xml 932 934 932 934 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
A caveat to the above described experiment is that the system utilises the lzGal4 enhancer to simultaneously monitor UAS-GFP expression and drive UAS-ttk69, when Ttk69, in turn, could then act to repress the lz enhancer element and no longer drive the UAS-ttk69 transgene. This experiment is therefore dependent upon the relative stability of Ttk69 in the third instar disc epithelium. While we did observe a perturbation to the development of differentiated lz-expressing cell types, it remains possible that lz-driven GFP expression was produced initially in undifferentiated cells before Ttk69 could be produced at high enough levels to repress lz. We therefore obtained a Lz antibody and examined Lz protein expression in discs where a Gal4 driver under the control of the glass multimer repeat (GMR) promoter was used to drive the UAS-ttk69 transgene in all cells posterior to the morphogenetic furrow in developing eye discs [55].
###end p 41
###begin p 42
###xml 12 15 12 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR</italic>
###xml 15 18 15 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal</italic>
###xml 15 19 15 19 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Gal</italic>4</sup>
###xml 231 233 231 233 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6I</xref>
###xml 407 409 407 409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6J</xref>
###xml 732 735 732 735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 1014 1020 1014 1020 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6I'-I"</xref>
###xml 1154 1157 1154 1157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6J'</xref>
###xml 1218 1221 1218 1221 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6J"</xref>
In control (GMRGal4;+) eye discs, a projected confocal image of all cells in the basal undifferentiated cell plane reveal that Lz is expressed in most, if not all, undifferentiated cells posterior to the morphogenetic furrow (fig. 6I). Upon Ttk69 overexpression, a marked reduction in the number of Lz expressing cells, and the levels of Lz expression, in the undifferentiated cell plane was observed (fig. 6J). Interestingly, Lz appeared to be expressed in a number of undifferentiated cells just posterior to the furrow, then expression decreased in the middle and posterior portions of the disc. This could simply reflect a delay in the onset of Ttk69 overexpression by the GMR-Gal4 transgene. Alternatively, Ttk69 could repress lz expression in specific pools of undifferentiated precursor cells. High magnification images of the middle disc region revealed that most, if not all, undifferentiated cells in control discs stained with the DNA marker 4',6-diamidino-2-phenylindole (Dapi) also expressed Lz (fig. 6I'-I"). In contrast, overexpression of Ttk69 in undifferentiated cells did not cause a reduction in the number of Dapi-stained cells (fig. 6J'), but a clear reduction of Lz expression was observed (fig. 6J").
###end p 42
###begin p 43
###xml 122 127 122 127 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6K, M</xref>
###xml 194 196 194 196 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 474 479 474 479 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6L, N</xref>
###xml 691 694 691 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
In the differentiated region of the control disc epithelia, Lz expression was observed in R1, R6, R7 and cone cells (fig. 6K, M). This is consistent with the published expression pattern of Lz [38], Additionally, we confirmed Lz antibody specificity by staining Lz null mutant disc epithelia with the antibody and observed no Lz expression (not shown). A reduction of Lz expression was observed in differentiated cells of disc epithelia where Ttk69 was over-expressed (fig. 6L, N). Very few cells expressing both Elav and Lz were ever observed in these developing eye discs, and few cone cells in the apical cell plane expressed Lz. Taken together, these results show that Ttk69 can repress lz expression in the developing eye.
###end p 43
###begin title 44
###xml 8 10 8 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 92 95 92 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 113 116 113 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
Loss of lz-dependent cells in Ttk69 overexpression flies can be rescued by expressing a GMR-lz transgene lacking lz regulatory regions
###end title 44
###begin p 45
###xml 72 75 72 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 124 126 124 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 269 271 269 271 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 377 384 377 384 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-lz </italic>
###xml 421 424 421 424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 491 494 491 494 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 547 549 547 549 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B34">34</xref>
###xml 573 592 573 592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 714 722 714 722 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz c3.5 </italic>
###xml 767 773 767 773 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-lz</italic>
###xml 983 994 983 994 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila </italic>
Our results have shown that Ttk69 overexpression leads to repression of lz expression, which in turn results in the loss of lz-dependent differentiating cell types in third instar eye disc epithelia. We next tested whether overexpression of Lz could rescue the loss of lz-dependent cells types observed from Ttk69 overexpression in developing eye discs. For this experiment, a GMR-lz transgene containing the full length lz 3.5 kb cDNA under the control of the GMR promoter, but lacking the lz eye specific enhancer and upstream promoter regions [34], was crossed into the GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 mutant background, and eye discs were analysed for the rescue of photoreceptors R1,6,7 and cone cells. By itself, the GMR-lz c3.5 transgene (referred to in subsequent text as GMR-lz) causes ectopic development of the presumptive R7 cell and a mild disorganisation of developing ommatidia (not shown), indicating that high levels of Lz expression can indeed promote the R7 cell fate early in Drosophila development.
###end p 45
###begin p 46
###xml 0 19 0 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 152 171 152 171 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 247 249 247 249 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6L</xref>
###xml 343 345 343 345 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 346 348 346 348 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 349 351 349 351 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B56">56</xref>
###xml 352 354 352 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B58">58</xref>
###xml 409 411 409 411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 458 484 458 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz </italic>
###xml 507 526 507 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 661 663 661 663 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7B</xref>
###xml 863 865 863 865 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7C</xref>
GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 adult eyes are severely perturbed, being devoid of any ommatidial structure (not shown). Furthermore, Elav labelling of third instar GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 eye discs showed that most neuronal cells failed to differentiate (see fig. 6L), which is not surprising given that Ttk69 is a general repressor of the neuronal cell fate [24,29,56-58]. We first used the Bar antibody to determine whether lz-dependent R1 and R6 cells could be rescued in GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz eye disc epithelia. In GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 eye discs, few Bar labelled cells were observed, with only 7.1% (N = 280) of ommatidia exhibiting at least one Bar positive cell (fig. 7B). Overexpression of Lz in the absence of the eye specific enhancer could partially alleviate this defect, with 32% of ommatidia (N = 312) showing the presence of at least one Bar positive cell (fig. 7C and inset).
###end p 46
###begin p 47
###xml 23 26 23 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 0 91 0 91 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">The expression of GMR- <italic>lz </italic>can rescue cellular defects caused by the overexpression of Ttk69</bold>
###xml 93 94 93 94 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>
###xml 204 205 204 205 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 247 253 247 253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk69 </italic>
###xml 260 261 260 261 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</bold>
###xml 318 323 318 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk69</italic>
###xml 328 331 328 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 342 343 342 343 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</bold>
###xml 447 455 441 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klingon </italic>
###xml 532 533 526 527 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</bold>
###xml 619 625 613 619 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk69 </italic>
###xml 636 637 630 631 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</bold>
###xml 713 718 704 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk69</italic>
###xml 723 726 714 717 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 811 812 802 803 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">G</bold>
###xml 894 895 885 886 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H</bold>
###xml 954 960 945 951 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk69 </italic>
###xml 967 968 958 959 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</bold>
###xml 1021 1026 1012 1017 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk69</italic>
###xml 1031 1034 1022 1025 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 1045 1046 1036 1037 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">J</bold>
###xml 1087 1088 1078 1079 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</bold>
###xml 1143 1149 1134 1140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk69 </italic>
###xml 1160 1161 1151 1152 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L</bold>
###xml 1232 1237 1223 1228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk69</italic>
###xml 1242 1245 1233 1236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
The expression of GMR- lz can rescue cellular defects caused by the overexpression of Ttk69. A. Imaging of Bar positive R1/R6 cells in wt eye discs. Inset in all panels shows higher magnification images. B. Bar expression is lost in GMR-Gal4; UAS-ttk69 discs. C. Partial rescue of R1/6 cells is shown in GMR-Gal4; UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz eye discs. D. Anti-beta-galactosidase (beta-gal) staining (red) of the Klingon-lacZ line (B38) shows high levels of klingon gene expression in R7 cells and lower expression levels in other cell types. E. B38 enhancer trap activity was only detected at background levels in GMR- Gal4; UAS-ttk69 eye discs. F. Partial rescue of beta-gal positive R7 cells is observed in GMR-Gal4; UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz eye discs. D-ECadherin staining (green) in D-F, and G-I was used to mark the furrow. G. Confocal image showing anti-Cut staining (red) of cone cells (CCs) in wt discs. H. Few Cut labelled CCs (red) are detected in GMR-Gal4; UAS-ttk69 discs. I. Partial rescue of CCs is observed in GMR-Gal4; UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz eye discs. J. Imaging of Pros labelled wt eye discs. K. Pros expression is markedly reduced in GMR-Gal4; UAS-ttk69 eye discs. L. A dramatic rescue of Pros in R7 and CCs is observed in GMR-Gal4; UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz eye discs. Scale Bars indicate 20 mum.
###end p 47
###begin p 48
###xml 50 75 50 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz</italic>
###xml 145 152 145 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-lz </italic>
###xml 183 202 183 202 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 265 273 265 273 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klingon </italic>
###xml 296 307 296 307 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila </italic>
###xml 376 378 376 378 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 483 485 483 485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 486 488 486 488 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B58">58</xref>
###xml 496 498 496 498 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7D</xref>
###xml 617 636 614 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 760 762 754 756 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7E</xref>
###xml 777 803 771 797 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR -Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz</italic>
###xml 915 917 906 908 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7F</xref>
To determine whether R7 cells could be rescued in GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz, the R7-specific enhancer trap line B38-LacZ was recombined with the GMR-lz transgene and crossed into the GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 background. The B38-LacZ line is an enhancer trap insertion in klingon (a novel member of the Drosophila immunoglobulin superfamily that is required for R7 cell development [57]) and is strongly expressed in R7 cells but only weakly expressed in other surrounding photoreceptors ([57,58]; fig. 7D). The use of an anti-beta-galactosidase antibody to detect enhancer trap activity showed the depletion of R7 cells in GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 eye discs, with as few as 3.9% of ommatidia (N = 310) ever showing the presence of a beta-galactosidase positive cell (fig. 7E). However, in GMR -Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz, many more beta-galactosidase positive R7 cells (69%; N = 362) were observed in the developing ommatidia (fig. 7F).
###end p 48
###begin p 49
###xml 73 75 73 75 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B59">59</xref>
###xml 83 85 83 85 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7G</xref>
###xml 139 158 139 158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 185 187 185 187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7H</xref>
###xml 246 272 246 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz </italic>
###xml 284 286 284 286 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7I</xref>
Non-neuronal cone cells can normally be detected with the Cut antibody ([59]; fig. 7G). While few Cut labelled cone cells were observed in GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 developing eye discs (fig. 7H), a proportion of Cut labelled cone cells were rescued in GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz discs (fig. 7I), although no ommatidia with the full complement of cone cells were ever observed. Due to the disorganisation of these cells, absolute numbers could not be obtained.
###end p 49
###begin p 50
###xml 8 13 8 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pros </italic>
###xml 44 46 44 46 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 107 133 107 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz </italic>
###xml 186 205 186 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 </italic>
###xml 221 223 221 223 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7K</xref>
###xml 238 264 238 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz </italic>
###xml 367 369 367 369 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7L</xref>
###xml 568 571 568 571 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 791 798 791 798 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-lz </italic>
###xml 814 817 814 817 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 882 885 882 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 926 928 926 928 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
Because pros is positively regulated by Lz [32], we asked whether Pros expression could also be rescued in GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz discs. Few Pros labelled cells were ever observed in GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69 eye discs (fig. 7K). However, in GMR-Gal4;UAS-ttk69/GMR-lz discs, a significant increase in Pros expression was observed, particularly in the R7 cell plane (fig. 7L). Taken together, these results strongly suggest that some of the cellular phenotypes observed upon Ttk69 overexpression in third instar developing eye disc are at least partially due to changes in lz expression, since the simultaneous overexpression of Lz and Ttk69 leads to rescue of R1,6,7 photoreceptors and non-neuronal cone cells, all of which are dependent upon Lz for fate specification. Furthermore, because the GMR-lz transgene lacks lz regulatory regions, these results suggest that the regulation of lz by Ttk69 could potentially occur via the lz-eye enhancer region.
###end p 50
###begin title 51
###xml 0 5 0 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina </italic>
###xml 9 13 9 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msi </italic>
sina and msi function as negative regulators of Ttk in R1/6/7 cells in early eye development
###end title 51
###begin p 52
###xml 68 73 68 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina </italic>
###xml 158 160 158 160 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 161 163 161 163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 164 166 164 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B60">60</xref>
###xml 234 236 234 236 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B61">61</xref>
###xml 486 488 486 488 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 586 595 586 595 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina msi </italic>
###xml 671 675 671 675 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msi </italic>
###xml 709 711 709 711 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 775 784 775 784 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina msi </italic>
###xml 804 807 804 807 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk</italic>
###xml 807 811 807 811 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">osn </italic>
###xml 807 811 807 811 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>osn </italic></sup>
The normal specification of the presumptive R7 cell is prevented in sina loss of function mutants due to failure of Ttk88, and presumably Ttk69, degradation [19,21,60]. However the expression pattern of Sina in R1,3,4,6 and R7 cells [61] initiated the investigation of the function of Sina in these other cell types. Genetic experiments have suggested that the RNA-binding protein Msi functions redundantly with Sina to down-regulate Ttk69 in R1 and R6 cells in larval eye development [27]. In their experiments, Hirota and colleagues showed the loss of R1, R6 and R7 photoreceptors in sina msi double loss of function mutants, while all cells were recruited properly in msi null mutant developing ommatidia [27]. Furthermore, 30% of retinal sections from adult ommatidia of sina msi double mutants in a ttkosn heterozygous mutant background, a mutation that disrupts both Ttk69 and Ttk88 protein expression, exhibited the correct number of photoreceptor neurons, consistent with the hypothesis of negative regulation of Ttk by both Sina and Msi.
###end p 52
###begin p 53
###xml 65 68 65 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 97 100 97 100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz </italic>
###xml 156 161 156 161 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina </italic>
###xml 203 212 203 212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina msi </italic>
###xml 254 256 254 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 256 259 256 259 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal</italic>
###xml 256 261 256 261 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Gal</italic>4 </sup>
###xml 318 323 318 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina </italic>
###xml 440 442 440 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 479 481 479 481 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8B</xref>
###xml 650 652 650 652 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8B</xref>
###xml 658 667 658 667 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina msi </italic>
###xml 700 702 700 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 778 780 778 780 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8C</xref>
###xml 948 953 948 953 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina </italic>
###xml 982 987 982 987 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8F-F'</xref>
###xml 997 1006 997 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina msi </italic>
###xml 1042 1047 1042 1047 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8G-G'</xref>
To further examine the relationship between Sina, Msi, Ttk69 and lz gene regulation, we examined lz gene expression in R1, R6 and R7 photoreceptor cells of sina loss of function mutant eye discs, and of sina msi double loss of function mutants using the lzGal4 enhancer trap line to drive GFP expression. Labelling of sina null mutant eye discs with the R1 and R6 photoreceptor marker Bar demonstrated that 87.2% of ommatidia contained two lz-expressing Bar positive cells (fig. 8B). However some ommatidia contained less than two Bar positive cells, indicating that Sina may play a minor role in the cell fate determination of R1 and R6 cells (fig. 8B). In sina msi double mutant eye discs very few lz-expressing Bar positive R1 and R6 cells were observed (1.2%, N = 250; fig. 8C). Analysis of R7-cell development in mutant eye discs with the presumptive R7 cell marker Runt showed that very few R7 cells are recruited to developing ommatitida in sina mutants (2.1%, N = 523; fig. 8F-F'), and in sina msi double mutants (.06%, N = 315; fig. 8G-G'). The possibility remains that fewer cells were recruited to differentiating ommatidia because fewer cells were available from the pool of undifferentiated cells.
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 0 92 0 92 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sina and Msi function as negative regulators of Ttk in R1/6/7 cells in early eye development</bold>

###xml 108 110 108 110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 110 114 110 114 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal4</sup>
###xml 168 169 168 169 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 174 178 174 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina</italic>
###xml 178 179 178 179 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 180 184 180 184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina</italic>

###xml 373 375 373 375 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>

###xml 400 404 400 404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina</italic>
###xml 404 405 404 405 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sup>
###xml 405 408 405 408 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msi</italic>
###xml 408 410 408 410 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1 </sup>
###xml 476 477 476 477 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</bold>
###xml 501 505 501 505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina</italic>
###xml 505 506 505 506 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 506 509 506 509 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msi</italic>

###xml 676 680 676 680 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal4</sup>
###xml 695 698 695 698 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ttk</italic>
###xml 698 702 698 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNAi</italic>
###xml 698 702 698 702 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>RNAi</italic></sup>
###xml 702 707 702 707 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">;sina</italic>
###xml 707 708 707 708 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 708 711 708 711 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msi</italic>
###xml 711 712 711 712 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sup>
###xml 713 717 713 717 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina</italic>
###xml 717 718 717 718 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sup>
###xml 718 721 718 721 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msi</italic>
###xml 721 723 721 723 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1 </sup>
###xml 748 749 748 749 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</bold>
###xml 803 805 803 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 805 809 805 809 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal4</sup>
###xml 908 910 908 910 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E'</bold>
###xml 991 994 991 994 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F-G</bold>
###xml 1025 1027 1025 1027 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 1027 1031 1027 1031 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal4</sup>
###xml 1041 1045 1041 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina</italic>
###xml 1045 1046 1045 1046 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 1047 1051 1047 1051 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina</italic>
###xml 1051 1053 1051 1053 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3 </sup>
###xml 1064 1068 1064 1068 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F-F'</bold>
###xml 1077 1079 1077 1079 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lz</italic>
###xml 1079 1083 1079 1083 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal4</sup>
###xml 1093 1097 1093 1097 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina</italic>
###xml 1097 1098 1097 1098 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 1098 1101 1098 1101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msi</italic>
###xml 1101 1102 1101 1102 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sup>
###xml 1103 1107 1103 1107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sina</italic>
